\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_array}{Array}

Generic base class for \doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_array}{Array} services. \doxylink{class_a}{A} \doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_array}{Array} can be used to generate and own a large collection of objects of the same type "{}\+T"{}. Objects are allocated on the heap and pointers "{}\+T\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}"{} to these objects kept in a large array T \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} objects. The array is nominally of fixed size but is enlarged whenever more objects are needed. The \doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_array}{Array} model is useful when objects need to be repeatedly used and discarded (e.\+g., in data analysis of particles) because no malloc or destroy is required. The memory remains allocated and so there is no time wasted creating and destroying the objects. The reset method is to be called on a \doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_array}{Array} to indicate that a new "{}event"{} is being considered. It must evidently be possible to initialize the objects with "{}set"{} methods specific to the class "{}\+T"{}. Use the T \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} next\+Object() method to obtain an used object.

\doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_factory}{Factory}

Generic base class for factory services. \doxylink{class_a}{A} factory can be used to generate and own a large collection of objects of the same type "{}\+T"{}. Objects are allocated on the heap and pointers "{}\+T\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}"{} to these objects kept in a large array T \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} objects. The array is nominally of fixed size but is enlarged whenever more objects are needed. The factory model is useful when objects need to be repeatedly used and discarded (e.\+g., in data analysis of particles) because no malloc or destroy is required. The memory remains allocated and so there is no time wasted creating and destroying the objects. The reset method is to be called on a factory to indicate that a new "{}event"{} is being considered. It must evidently be possible to initialize the objects with "{}set"{} methods specific to the class "{}\+T"{}. Use the T \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} next\+Object() method to obtain an used object.

Compendium of physics constants By convention, all function names begin with a lower case letter. Instead of naming function after the letter commonly used in the literature e.\+g., c for the speed of light, functions are named after what they represent to avoid ambiguities and naming crounding. For instance, instead of "{}c"{} for the speed of light, we use "{}light\+Velocity"{}

\doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_object_list}{Object\+List}

\doxylink{class_a}{A} named list (std::\+vector) of objects The objects can be of any types "{}\+T"{} The list can be given a name and a title (or description) via the \doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_object}{Object} class

Compendium of basic and essential mathematical functions By convention, all function names begin with a lower case letter.

Compendium of basic geometry and vector functions By convention, all function names begin with a lower case letter.

Compendium of sorting functions By convention, all function names begin with a lower case letter.

Compendium of basic mathematical constants

The Vector3 class encapuslate physical 3D vectors.

It is templated to enable different types of storage. Some functions are only meaningfull in 3 or 4 dimensions. If called for lower dimension, they throw an exception of type Math\+Exception.

storage\+Type for 3D 0 :\+ x, y, z (cartesian coordinates) 1 :\+ phi, theta, r (spherical coordinates) 2 :\+ phi, rho, z (cylindrical coordinates)

\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_aba1a5e8e5bbd02eaffaa52e9b6fbe891}\index{CAP@{CAP}!calculateAverage@{calculateAverage}}
\index{calculateAverage@{calculateAverage}!CAP@{CAP}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{calculateAverage()}{calculateAverage()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_aba1a5e8e5bbd02eaffaa52e9b6fbe891} 
void CAP::\+calculate\+Average (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} \&}]{avg\+Density}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} \&}]{e\+Avg\+Density}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Compute the average density of particles based on the given d\+N/\+dx histogram. The histogram is assumed to be a yield per event per bin vs. eta The average value is thus divided by the bin width to make it into a density. This yields a density integrated over 2pi. So to use this number, one must also divide by 2pi. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_a96b763862d9655e87f6f79befd8885b2}\index{CAP@{CAP}!calculateAverageVsDeta@{calculateAverageVsDeta}}
\index{calculateAverageVsDeta@{calculateAverageVsDeta}!CAP@{CAP}}

\index{differenceHistograms@{differenceHistograms}!CAP@{CAP}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{differenceHistograms()}{differenceHistograms()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_a5960162787076248294dde1b5e6c42cf} 
void CAP::\+difference\+Histograms (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h1}{, }\item[{const TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h2}{, }\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{difference}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

difference = h1 -\/ h2 \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_a2d15ed7e594e86f0afdea313632766eb}\index{CAP@{CAP}!differenceHistos@{differenceHistos}}
\index{differenceHistos@{differenceHistos}!CAP@{CAP}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{differenceHistos()}{differenceHistos()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_a2d15ed7e594e86f0afdea313632766eb} 
void CAP::\+difference\+Histos (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h}{, }\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+Ref}{, }\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+Diff}{, }\item[{bool}]{correlated\+Uncertainties}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Span all bins of h and href and calculate the content difference (and the uncertainty) and store the difference in h\+Diff. All three given histograms must have the same exact dimensions. The histogram h and h\+Ref may be profiles. Uncertainties on the difference h\+Diff are computed as sum of square of uncertainties on h and href if correlated\+Uncertainties==0 and as a difference of square of uncertainties if correlated\+Uncertainties==1.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em h} & Histogram to be tested against the reference Histogram \\
\hline
{\em h\+Ref} & Reference Histogram \\
\hline
{\em h\+Diff} & Difference histogram produced on output \\
\hline
{\em correlated\+Uncertainties} & Whether the uncertainties of h and href are correlated:\+ true if they are, false if they are not. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_a84da7fc8387395d77c94f8a9e2c2fd29}\index{CAP@{CAP}!divideHistograms@{divideHistograms}}
\index{divideHistograms@{divideHistograms}!CAP@{CAP}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{divideHistograms()}{divideHistograms()}}

\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} CAP::\+hermite\+\_\+func\+\_\+series (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \doxymbox{\hyperlink{legendre__source_8cpp_a9edd8b6d7decf3f5e76044956985631a}{int}}}]{n}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{a}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Evaluates the series sum\+\_\+\{j=0\}\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}n a\+\_\+j\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\+Psi\+\_\+j(x) with Psi\+\_\+j being the j-\/th Hermite function. for improved numerical stability the Clenshaw algorithm (Clenshaw, C. W. (July 1955). "{}\+A note on the summation of Chebyshev series"{}. Mathematical Tables and other Aids to Computation 9 (51):\+ 118–110.) adapted to Hermite functions is used. \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}/\+ \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_afaa1f73308e803288e3ece8c92e4d324}\index{CAP@{CAP}!hermite\_prob\_zero@{hermite\_prob\_zero}}

\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_ac066b3fa82480e5b5b03ee0beb13690f}\index{CAP@{CAP}!ratioHistos@{ratioHistos}}
\index{ratioHistos@{ratioHistos}!CAP@{CAP}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ratioHistos()}{ratioHistos()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_ac066b3fa82480e5b5b03ee0beb13690f} 
void CAP::\+ratio\+Histos (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h}{, }\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+Ref}{, }\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+Diff}{, }\item[{bool}]{correlated\+Uncertainties}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Span all bins of h and href and calculate the content ratio (and the uncertainty) and store the ratio in h\+Ratio. All three given histograms must have the same exact dimensions. The histogram h and h\+Ref may be profiles. Uncertainties on the difference h\+Ratio are computed as sum of square of uncertainties on h and href if correlated\+Uncertainties==0 and as a difference of square of uncertainties if correlated\+Uncertainties==1.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em h} & Histogram to be tested against the reference Histogram \\
\hline
{\em h\+Ref} & Reference Histogram \\
\hline
{\em h\+Diff} & Ratio histogram produced on output \\
\hline
{\em correlated\+Uncertainties} & Whether the uncertainties of h and href are correlated:\+ true if they are, false if they are not. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_a0d97fbe571ac818331956ead019b676b}\index{CAP@{CAP}!reduce\_n1EtaPhiN1EtaPhiOntoN1N1DetaDphi@{reduce\_n1EtaPhiN1EtaPhiOntoN1N1DetaDphi}}
\index{reduce\_n1EtaPhiN1EtaPhiOntoN1N1DetaDphi@{reduce\_n1EtaPhiN1EtaPhiOntoN1N1DetaDphi}!CAP@{CAP}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{reduce\_n1EtaPhiN1EtaPhiOntoN1N1DetaDphi()}{reduce\_n1EtaPhiN1EtaPhiOntoN1N1DetaDphi()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_c_a_p_a0d97fbe571ac818331956ead019b676b} 
void CAP::\+reduce\+\_\+n1\+Eta\+Phi\+N1\+Eta\+Phi\+Onto\+N1\+N1\+Deta\+Dphi (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const TH2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+\_\+1}{, }\item[{TH2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+\_\+2}{, }\item[{TH2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+\_\+12}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{legendre__source_8cpp_a9edd8b6d7decf3f5e76044956985631a}{int}}}]{n\+Deta}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{legendre__source_8cpp_a9edd8b6d7decf3f5e76044956985631a}{int}}}]{n\+Dphi}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Calculate the external product of n\+\_\+1(eta,phi) by n\+\_\+2(eta,phi) and project onto n1n1\+\_\+12(\+Deta,\+Dphi) First create a 4D external product of h\+\_\+1 and h\+\_\+2 using a 1D std::\+vector than project it onto Delta\+Eta(x-\/axis) Delta\+Phi (y-\/axis) Errors are neglected and must be accounted for using a sub-\/sample analysis. \Hypertarget{namespace_c_a_p_a1e02565eb9c60f910aa9d5c01c790de3}\index{CAP@{CAP}!reduce\_n2xEtaPhi\_n2DetaDphi@{reduce\_n2xEtaPhi\_n2DetaDphi}}

void CAP::\+square\+Difference\+Histos (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h\+Avg}{, }\item[{TH1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{h}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{sum\+Weights}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{alf_8hpp_a8c979c7f1bf8ea6722258adaba7b30b5}{double}}}]{weight}{, }\item[{\doxymbox{\hyperlink{legendre__source_8cpp_a9edd8b6d7decf3f5e76044956985631a}{int}}}]{n}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Span all bins of h\+Avg and h and compute the difference between histo "{}h"{} and the reference "{}havg"{}, and increment the value havg accordingly. \doxylink{class_c_a_p_1_1_histogram_group}{Histogram\+Group} must have the same exact dimensions. The histograms may be profiles.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em h\+Avg} & Histogram containing the running average \\
\hline
{\em h} & Histogram to be compared to h\+Avg and use to update the average and the uncertainties. \\
\hline
{\em sum\+Weights} & Cumulated sum of weights \\
\hline
{\em weight} & Weight given to histogram h. \\
\hline
{\em n} & Index of file being processed. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
